        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2284442852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15080643309214674375">4.5/5<br/><br/>(Reseña en español debajo)<br/><br/>My problem with science fiction is the freedom of the authors to use words referring to physical phenomena to describe a certain technology. For those who do not know, I have a degree and a PhD in physics, and the nerd in me can not avoid to think about how that technology would work, so I usually spend a lot of time frustrating myself because I can not find the meaning. Something like that happened to me with Hyperion, by Dan Simmons.<br/>However, although Asimov left </span>
  <span id="freeText15080643309214674375" style="display:none">4.5/5<br /><br />(Reseña en español debajo)<br /><br />My problem with science fiction is the freedom of the authors to use words referring to physical phenomena to describe a certain technology. For those who do not know, I have a degree and a PhD in physics, and the nerd in me can not avoid to think about how that technology would work, so I usually spend a lot of time frustrating myself because I can not find the meaning. Something like that happened to me with Hyperion, by Dan Simmons.<br />However, although Asimov left me thinking for a while with some artifacts, in general the narrative has focused on aspects such as the personality of several characters in this trilogy. I thought it was a wonderful book, which I could not stop reading. It is really fascinating to read about the development of the Foundation during the years of anarchy, and I definitely want to read much more about this author. There is not a minute of boredom.<br />Since the saga of the Foundation takes several centuries, we do not see the point of view of a few characters, but several generations are the ones who tell us this story, people with different personalities and motivations.<br />I really recommend it a lot.<br /><br />Mi problema con la ciencia ficción, es la libertad de quienes la escriben de utilizar palabras referidas a fenómenos físicos para describir una determinada tecnología. Para quienes no lo saben, tengo un grado y un doctorado en física, y la nerd en mí no puede evitar ponerse a pensar cómo esa tecnología funcionaría, por lo que suelo pasar mucho tiempo frustrándome por no poder encontrarle el sentido. Algo así me pasó con Hyperion, de Dan Simmons.<br />Sin embargo, aunque Asimov me dejó pensando un buen rato con algunos artefactos, en general la narración se ha enfocado en aspectos como la personalidad de varios personajes de esta trilogía. Me ha parecido un libro maravilloso, al que no podía parar de leer. Es realmente fascinante acompañar al desarrollo de la Fundación durante los años de anarquía, y definitivamente tengo ganas de leer mucho más de este autor. No hay un minuto de aburrimiento.<br />Dado que la saga de la Fundación ocupa varios siglos, no vemos el punto de vista de unos pocos personajes, sino que varias generaciones son las que nos cuentan esta historia, personas con diferentes personalidades y motivaciones.<br />Realmente lo recomiendo muchísimo.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15080643309214674375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_358397869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358397869" />
    <a title="Andy Wenman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10586591-andy-wenman"><img alt="Andy Wenman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357018189p2/10586591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358397869?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Wenman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Wenman" href="/user/show/10586591-andy-wenman">Andy Wenman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358397869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11992961871617506555">I read some short stories by Asimov in High-School and although he never measured up to the likes Rohald Dahl or Kurt Vonnegut I seem to remember actually enjoying some of them, but there's no way I can pretend that this novel was anything other than awful. This is bad science fiction in every sense of the word, overly descriptive of irrelevant details, filled soulless characters all with the same emotionless analytical voice, events that seem to have no purpose and all take place in a world tha</span>
  <span id="freeText11992961871617506555" style="display:none">I read some short stories by Asimov in High-School and although he never measured up to the likes Rohald Dahl or Kurt Vonnegut I seem to remember actually enjoying some of them, but there's no way I can pretend that this novel was anything other than awful. This is bad science fiction in every sense of the word, overly descriptive of irrelevant details, filled soulless characters all with the same emotionless analytical voice, events that seem to have no purpose and all take place in a world that's extremely difficult to contextualise and even harder to care about and written with no style or eye for pacing. I read at least half of the book and I honestly can't tell you what was happening, who any of the characters were or what was at stake. This is one of those books that is so uninteresting it's actually infuriating. Great science fiction uses the conceits of the genre to deal with big philosophical and questions and confront socio-political constructs, but it makes the reader care about these issues by putting a relatable character with basic human dilemmas at the centre. This is where Foundation fails, it's all ideas and no humanity. I'd love to disseminate it more, but honestly, who cares? Who the fuck even cares? Do not recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11992961871617506555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5434098-kyle?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5434098-kyle?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5434098-kyle?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5434098-kyle?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5434098-kyle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer446961269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6089184203674165328">The Foundation Trilogy is widely considered one of the most influential science fiction series ever written - it even won a Hugo award for the best all-time series back in the 60's.<br/><br/>And I get it. I can see why it's so influential, mostly because I've read and seen the books and movies and television shows that have been influenced by it (I'm mostly talking about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy___1_' title='The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy, #1) by Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a> and <i>Futurama</i>, but there are countless others). Isaac Asimov has so many fantastic, interesting idea</span>
  <span id="freeText6089184203674165328" style="display:none">The Foundation Trilogy is widely considered one of the most influential science fiction series ever written - it even won a Hugo award for the best all-time series back in the 60's.<br /><br />And I get it. I can see why it's so influential, mostly because I've read and seen the books and movies and television shows that have been influenced by it (I'm mostly talking about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy___1_" title="The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy, #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a> and <i>Futurama</i>, but there are countless others). Isaac Asimov has so many fantastic, interesting ideas - he's tracing the fall and rise of a civilization, using past history to guide him. In the span of three novels we've seen this history play out over 400 years, and seen how people originally seen as minor players were revered down in history later on.<br /><br />It's just that it's <i>so</i> dry. Seriously. I realize that the ideas are more important than the writing, but this is a book. I need more than interesting ideas to keep me motivated to read.<br /><br />The books do get better, however, I will admit that. But <i>Foundation</i>, the first book in the series, is hard to get over. I took a four month hiatus in between that and the second book because I couldn't get over how dry it was. Seriously, <i>Foundation</i> consists of people sitting around talking about ideas. All the action happens off the stage, and we're left to hear people discuss ideas. I get that Asimov is telling a broad history, and that history is more influenced by backroom politicking than different battles, but I wish he had given us something. And since the novel takes place over quite a long period, I never really felt like I had the time to devote much attention or interest in any particular character.<br /><br />Asimov definitely picks up the pace in <i>Foundation and Empire</i>. While the first half is reminiscent of <i>Foundation</i>, he at least seems aware of this fact, and has one of his characters comment on the absurd amount of talking everybody does. But it's the second half, about the Mule, where things really get interesting. This is the story that deviates from intended purpose of the series, where one man with abnormal capabilities disrupts the plan and a small band of people have to join together to defeat him. There was still quite a bit of talking, but it was spliced in between action and characters having to make important decisions in order to save the whole galaxy while on the run from a great evil. Bayta Darrell and The Mule are interesting, flawed characters who grow and change. Bayta especially is one of the most clever people in the series, and I wish that she had appeared in more than just this book - she's clever enough to match wits with any science fiction hero, and she's able to use her inherent goodness against the most manipulative of foes.<br /><br /><i>Second Foundation</i> was my favorite book of the series. Asimov still reverted to talking, but there was far less of it. Besides, this book also introduces us to the first truly funny character in the series: Arkady Darrell, who is mostly funny by the virtue of her being 14 and who gains all of her knowledge from books and television stories about spies and other romance stories. This is not a new character archetype - Don Quixote is the most famous, but there are many others. And it's a lot of fun to see Arkady go from a naive 14-year old girl, obsessed with living out the roles in her books and movies like any true hero to a 14-year old girl who understands that the world is an incredibly dangerous place and that her actions can cause great harm to a lot of the people she holds near and dear. It's the most true journey of any character presented in this series (so far), and it's incredibly rewarding. I'd go back and read about Arkady any day, though I'd probably skip the last chapter.<br /><br />I get what Asimov was trying to do with the Foundation series. And there are times, when he moves away from the archetypical science fiction hero who is right and doesn't really have any sort of interesting journey to characters who learn and grow and change, that he really succeeds. And while the last half of <i>Foundation and Empire</i> and almost all of <i>Second Foundation</i> are worth it, I just can't get over the first book and a half. <br /><br />I'm glad I read it, because now I get so many of the references that I see in other science fiction series, but I don't know that I'd ever reread it; I certainly wouldn't reread all of it. But when I inevitably reread <i>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</i> and its sequels, at least I'll have a better understanding of the jokes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6089184203674165328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I'm sure that, were I to pick it up once more, my appreciation would grow exponentially... HOWEVER, as wonderful as Asimov is, he writes like an engineer. He's careful and methodical, and the plot that weaves through the <i>Foundation</i> series is unbelievably complex. If you've got the time, and you enjoy Sci-fi, go ahead and pick up Prelude and follow Hari's awesome adventure.</span>

<div id="review_2757748911" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2757748911" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2757748911?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307593962" href="/book/show/7932877-foundation-foundation-and-empire-second-foundation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2757748911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15794585185845802763">Isaac Asimov's Foundation trilogy ranks up there, IMHO, with Frank Herbert's Dune in terms of being a pillar of the sci-fi community. Strangely I had read this series when I was young and then encountered it again in later. The concepts behind Hari Seldon's mathematical interpretation of groups of people acting in predictable patterns to be intriguing. In time, that concept grew on me and actually had a practical application in my Intelligence work and then, post-military, during my PhD work. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText15794585185845802763" style="display:none">Isaac Asimov's Foundation trilogy ranks up there, IMHO, with Frank Herbert's Dune in terms of being a pillar of the sci-fi community. Strangely I had read this series when I was young and then encountered it again in later. The concepts behind Hari Seldon's mathematical interpretation of groups of people acting in predictable patterns to be intriguing. In time, that concept grew on me and actually had a practical application in my Intelligence work and then, post-military, during my PhD work. The seed planted by Asimov had germinated, over the course of a decade or two, into my doctoral research into the mathematical interpretations of conflict. So I am, obviously, fond of this series.<br /><br />My copy by the Everyman's Library was rather nice. It has all three books here: Foundation, Foundation and Empire and Second Foundation. The series starts with Foundation. The Galactic Empire has stood for millennia. Spread across millions of worlds it is an entity that seems built for eternity. Such is not the case, as proven by a brilliant scientist named Hari Seldon. Realizing that individuals are exceedingly difficult to predict, he starts to calculate probabilities for mass movements. Essentially "herd theory".<br /><br />But Seldon's warnings are either misunderstood or ignored by the powers that be. So Seldon founds two Foundations. One on a small planet called Terminus and a mysterious Second Foundation that is mentioned only in passing. The story then follows the events on the tiny planet of Terminus and we see the Foundation struggle to survive. As time passes the Foundation, which has managed to keep all science and technology unlike the decaying Empire, grows in power and attracts the attention of nearby powers. These existential threats, Seldon Crisis, are then dealt with- in the first case by the Mayor Salvor Hardin. We also learn in the first book, the bare hints at a Second Foundation.<br /><br />The 2nd book is Foundation and Empire. In this the last great Imperial General launches an assault on Terminus and is defeated, but the greater part of the book is about the Mule. The Mule is a mutant and thus outside the mathematics of Seldon's Plan. The Mule is opposed by Toran and Bataya Darell and Ebling Mis. The Mule comes to conquer the First Foundation and seeks the Second.<br /><br />The 3rd Book is Second Foundation which covers the Mule's attempt to find the location of and destroy the Second Foundartion. It also reveals where the Second Foundation is located and its abilities.<br /><br />I have tried to be vague and not give away any spoilers since this is a book you should read for yourself. Clever, fast paced and with some great characters this is a series that will keep you wanting more. It truly does deserve a place amongst the best sci-fi stories out there.<br /><br />Highly recommended for any fan of sci-fi or even just a very good story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15794585185845802763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10044598999774953754">Devo dirlo: l'ho finito, finalmente! È una lettura difficile e ci vuole tanta volontà per completarla e rimanere concentrati, nel mentre ho letto anche un saggio di Stephen Hawking proprio perché volevo comprendere a grandi linee i concetti dell'astrofisica, infatti Asimov tratta velatamente anche concetti come il funzionamento dei fotoni, dei quanti, ecco giusto per sottolineare che non è una lettura banale e che suscita molta curiosità. <br/>Ho dovuto pensarci molto in merito alle stelline, quattro</span>
  <span id="freeText10044598999774953754" style="display:none">Devo dirlo: l'ho finito, finalmente! È una lettura difficile e ci vuole tanta volontà per completarla e rimanere concentrati, nel mentre ho letto anche un saggio di Stephen Hawking proprio perché volevo comprendere a grandi linee i concetti dell'astrofisica, infatti Asimov tratta velatamente anche concetti come il funzionamento dei fotoni, dei quanti, ecco giusto per sottolineare che non è una lettura banale e che suscita molta curiosità. <br />Ho dovuto pensarci molto in merito alle stelline, quattro, ma spesso ne volevo mettere due o tre, e qualche volta volevo abbandonare la lettura (raramente mi è accaduto). <br />Parla di politica, di accordi impliciti ed espliciti e questo argomento non mi piace molto, quasi lo detesto ma fa parte della vita umana, anche tra 10000 a quanto pare 😱<br />Una pecca, è stato scritto negli anni 50 e quindi la tecnologia futuristica è un po' troppo cartacea, Asimov oggi potrebbe apporre delle correzioni più smart, videochiamate, messaggi non di carta, giornali non di carta, ma si sa.. chi avrebbe pensato che questo famigerati "quanti" avessero cambiato radicalmente l'evoluzione tecnologica in pochi decenni. <br />Concludo, non sottovalutate la lettura e non portatela sotto l'ombrellone (qui non ci sono battaglie, amori o belle donne) ma leggetela seriamente. <br /><br />Ps Bisogna leggere l'intera trilogia altrimenti si perde molto, in questa edizione Mondadori ha un po' stritolato le secondo me 800 pagine rendendole 550 trasformando il volume in una dimensione più "commestibile", i caratteri rimangono grandi ma l'interlinea è un po' schiacciata e quindi ci si accorge che le pagine sarebbero state un po' di più, comunque complimenti perché se era più voluminoso avrebbe spaventato molti</span>

<div id="review_557204847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/557204847" />
    <a title="Ralph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8297770-ralph"><img alt="Ralph" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/557204847?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ralph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ralph" href="/user/show/8297770-ralph">Ralph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9788499083209" href="/book/show/12824455-trilog-a-de-la-fundaci-n">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer557204847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7940773638310734754">La verdad es que es un libro bastante extenso (900 páginas de nada) y hay que empezarlo con ganas porque de lo contrario es muy posible que dejes la historia. Lo que sí os digo es que el osado lector que se atreva con el tocho de libro no desmerecerá su esfuerzo ya que, a medida que avanzas en la trama, te vas enganchando y solo deseas saber cómo acaba la historia. <br/>	En cuanto al autor, lo considero un genio, solo hay que ver lo que escribió y cómo lo escribió. Esta saga es de los años 50 y le da</span>
  <span id="freeText7940773638310734754" style="display:none">La verdad es que es un libro bastante extenso (900 páginas de nada) y hay que empezarlo con ganas porque de lo contrario es muy posible que dejes la historia. Lo que sí os digo es que el osado lector que se atreva con el tocho de libro no desmerecerá su esfuerzo ya que, a medida que avanzas en la trama, te vas enganchando y solo deseas saber cómo acaba la historia. <br />	En cuanto al autor, lo considero un genio, solo hay que ver lo que escribió y cómo lo escribió. Esta saga es de los años 50 y le da mil vueltas a muchos libros y autores de hoy en día. <br />	Del libro me ha gustado el tema: una ciencia que puede predecir estadísticamente el devenir de una humanidad extendida por millones de planetas de la Galaxia y que ha creado un gran Imperio Galáctico. Ante un futuro descorazonador se decide crear una Fundación que proteja para la posteridad el conocimiento desarrollado por la humanidad durante millones de años. Esta es la causa, el motivo de toda la historia pero, al ir avanzando descubres otra realidad, subyacente, y sería la capacidad de controlar mentalmente el avance de miles de millones de personas siguiendo un Plan preestablecido y marcado y solo conocido por una élite que se oculta al resto de la Humanidad para que no se altere dicho Plan. Una idea muy interesante y original sobre la manipulación. Una obra que deberían leer los seguidores de la teoría de la Conspiración.<br />Hay mucha información en la red sobre este autor y la saga de la Fundación. Yo destaco aquí las citas del libro:<br />•	En boca de Salvor Hardin, en su libro Fundación:<br />o	"La violencia es el último recurso del incompetente".<br />o	"Nunca permitas que el sentido de la moral te impida hacer lo que está bien".<br />o	"Vale la pena ser obvio, especialmente si eres famoso por tu sutileza."<br />o	"Para tener éxito, la planificación sola es insuficiente. Uno debe improvisar también."<br />o	"Solamente una mentira que no esté avergonzada de sí misma puede tener posibilidades de éxito."<br />o	"Una pistola atómica puede disparar en dos direcciones".<br />Y os dejo una pequeña muestra de lo que se puede encontrar en la red de este genio de la ciencia ficción que, desgraciadamente, se está convirtiendo en todo un extraño para las nuevas generaciones.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://frikicaos.wordpress.com/2010/07/23/isaac-asimov-saga-la-fundacion/">http://frikicaos.wordpress.com/2010/0...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ciencia-ficcion.com/autores/asimovi.htm">http://www.ciencia-ficcion.com/autore...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://es.wikiquote.org/wiki/Isaac_Asimov">http://es.wikiquote.org/wiki/Isaac_As...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.laflecha.net/perfiles/ciencia/isaac_asimov">http://www.laflecha.net/perfiles/cien...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.asimovonline.com/asimov_home_page.html">http://www.asimovonline.com/asimov_ho...</a> en inglés<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.asimovs.com/info/links.shtml">http://www.asimovs.com/info/links.shtml</a> interesantes links de ciencia ficción<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mimundo-nerea.blogspot.com.es/2011/06/trilogia-de-la-fundacion-resena-de-la.html">http://mimundo-nerea.blogspot.com.es/...</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7940773638310734754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1345628025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1345628025" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43958421-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533937262p2/43958421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1345628025?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/43958421-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788804528647" href="/book/show/9646839-trilogia-della-fondazione">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1345628025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7577882467800248032"><b> Non avevo mai letto Asimov prima d'ora.<br/>Non avevo mai letto fantascienza prima d'ora. </b><br/><br/>Il mio battesimo di fuoco mi ha trovata impreparata storicamente al genere, eppure ha visto in me un'appassionata lettrice. Mi pento di aver nutrito tanti pregiudizi verso lo stesso, in passato, ma abbiate pietà: la filmografia fantascientifica esula dal correlato genere lettererario, fatta eccezione per qualche pellicola.<br/><br/>Dunque, sfatato il mito della fantascienza tutta <i> umanoidi-e-razzi-orbitanti-ultrametallic</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7577882467800248032" style="display:none"><b> Non avevo mai letto Asimov prima d'ora.<br />Non avevo mai letto fantascienza prima d'ora. </b><br /><br />Il mio battesimo di fuoco mi ha trovata impreparata storicamente al genere, eppure ha visto in me un'appassionata lettrice. Mi pento di aver nutrito tanti pregiudizi verso lo stesso, in passato, ma abbiate pietà: la filmografia fantascientifica esula dal correlato genere lettererario, fatta eccezione per qualche pellicola.<br /><br />Dunque, sfatato il mito della fantascienza tutta <i> umanoidi-e-razzi-orbitanti-ultrametallicamente-moderni </i> posso dire di aver ampliato il mio portfolio di letture in maniera più che soddisfacente, e di voler continuare in questa direzione. <br /><br />Fatta questa premessa, ho trovato Asimov un uomo fantasioso.<br />Dei tre libri ho preferito il secondo, "Fondazione e Impero", sull'interregno del Mule negli anni trascorsi alla ricerca della Seconda Fondazione. Credo di averlo preferito per un semplice e ragionevole motivo: mi sono innamorata di <b> Magnifico </b>. <br />Non è il solito romanticismo femminile, l'istinto da madre-crocerossina che genera sentimenti di tenerezza verso individui brutti, dinoccolati, il registro ottocentesco e gli occhietti tristi. Me ne sono innamorata alla fine, verso le ultime pagine, per motivi che non posso ben delineare, pena lo spoiler su uno degli avvenimenti più travolgenti e intriganti del libro [personalmente, dell'intera trilogia]. Sono sincera, mi aspettavo una "Seconda Fondazione" in cui fosse impiegato in maniera differente, ma va bene così. Mi trovo ancora troppo legata ai singoli personaggi, più che alle masse.<br /><br />Sarei, in una vita futura, una pessima psicostoriografa: lontana anni-luce dal poter divenire Oratrice.<br />Se non in tempo di crisi.<br /><br />N.B.: Sconsiglio altamente di leggere la trilogia nella stessa edizione che ho letto io. Errori -voglio sperare- di battitura a iosa: punteggiatura dilaniata e, molto spesso, letterine mancate o mostruosamente aggiunte [vedi "provincie"]. Ripongo la mia fiducia nella infinita distrazione di colui o coloro che hanno provveduto alla stampa -e alla revisione, soprattutto- e vi consiglio di sceglierne un'altra, di edizione. Il libro si legge comunque tutto d'un fiato, ma per un grammafanatico come me sono inevitabili certe fitte allo stomaco e al cervello.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7577882467800248032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2211217828722417729" style="display:none">La dificultad que os podéis encontrar, si queréis leer toda la Saga de la Fundación, estriba en no dejar pasar demasiado tiempo entre la lectura de los diferentes volúmenes, pues se olvidan muchos detalles de las diferentes tramas que son básicos para comprender lo que ocurre en los siguientes libros y llegar a hacerse una idea de la larga historia del Imperio Galáctico. También se pueden leer solo algunos libros como si fuesen novelas independientes, pues cada una tiene su argumento, sus personajes y su final definido, si bien todas están relacionadas. En cambio, si os interesa, recomiendo leer estas tres de la Trilogía original enteras y por su orden.<br /><br />Crítica completa en: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://alibreria.com/2017/04/07/introduccion-a-la-fundacion-de-isaac-asimov/">https://alibreria.com/2017/04/07/intr...</a></span>

<div id="review_1431286121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1431286121" />
    <a title="George Jankovic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48492241-george-jankovic"><img alt="George Jankovic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492530766p2/48492241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1431286121?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="George Jankovic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="George Jankovic" href="/user/show/48492241-george-jankovic">George Jankovic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48492241-george-jankovic?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1431286121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16172579441996930731">What can I say except THE BEST scifi books. I've read the Foundation books several times and, each time, I felt the same way. I got my son hooked on them too. He read the whole series at the age of 11 and loved them. I recommend it to people of all ages. <br/><br/>P.S. I always hoped (and still do) that I will make psychohistory a reality. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49006581" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49006581" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/646953-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297712338p2/646953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49006581?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/646953-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/646953-patrick?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/646953-patrick?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49006581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10948569065352651537">Am rereading these after 30+ years. The first still has the compelling ideas of psychohistory, although less developed than I had remembered, or would have liked. To Azimov's credit, the character of the Mule was still vivid enough in my memory that the second book lost most of its tension.<br/><br/>What I had forgotten was just how virulently misogynist and patriarchal these books are - it is kind of embarrassing given that he came of age when women had been working in factories, serving in war, and hold</span>
  <span id="freeText10948569065352651537" style="display:none">Am rereading these after 30+ years. The first still has the compelling ideas of psychohistory, although less developed than I had remembered, or would have liked. To Azimov's credit, the character of the Mule was still vivid enough in my memory that the second book lost most of its tension.<br /><br />What I had forgotten was just how virulently misogynist and patriarchal these books are - it is kind of embarrassing given that he came of age when women had been working in factories, serving in war, and holding families together on their own. Their depiction as silly, vain, and useless seems adolescent at best. I remembered <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/205.Robert_A__Heinlein" title="Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert A. Heinlein</a> being a militaristic jerk, but had a more romantic image of Azimov. Re-reading this series has altered that view. E.g., in Azimov's future, society has somehow become race-less (if not all-white), nicely matching the purely decorative role for women.<br /><br />Having recently re-read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/222093.City" title="City by Clifford D. Simak" rel="nofollow noopener">City</a>, and considering that a young Azimov should have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/266110.Vannevar_Bush" title="Vannevar Bush" rel="nofollow noopener">Vannevar Bush</a>, it is also embarrassing how quaint is his depiction of a galactic future where messages are still passed on paper, all history is on microfilm and in physical libraries, etc. That everyone smokes all the time is just silly. Asimov says he read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23012.Clifford_D__Simak" title="Clifford D. Simak" rel="nofollow noopener">Clifford D. Simak</a>, and yet somehow completely missed his remarkable prescience in areas of technology, communications, media, social evolution, etc.<br /><br />To call this a trilogy is disingenuous - it would have been only a moderately long novel as one, and each part would be completely unsatisfying on its own. <br /><br />All in all, disappointing as a re-read (I changed from 5 stars in my memory to just 3 now). There are still some great ideas in here, but maybe you just have to be very young, and enthralled with space to overlook the faults.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10948569065352651537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7996436" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7996436" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/300186-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403347993p2/300186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7996436?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/300186-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345312051" href="/book/show/776540.The_Foundation_Trilogy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7996436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6544483166381711790">A great premise and a good read, but I think Asimov makes a wrong turn half-way through the Trilogy. Here's the set up: it is many thousands of years in the future, humanity has colonized the universe, and for 12,000 years, the Galactic Empire has reigned. A man called Hari Seldon, however, develops the science of psychohistory, and with it comes to predict the fall of the Empire and the coming of 30,000 years of chaos. He establishes the Foundation, a colony on the edge of the Empire, in such a</span>
  <span id="freeText6544483166381711790" style="display:none">A great premise and a good read, but I think Asimov makes a wrong turn half-way through the Trilogy. Here's the set up: it is many thousands of years in the future, humanity has colonized the universe, and for 12,000 years, the Galactic Empire has reigned. A man called Hari Seldon, however, develops the science of psychohistory, and with it comes to predict the fall of the Empire and the coming of 30,000 years of chaos. He establishes the Foundation, a colony on the edge of the Empire, in such a way that historical forces will likely push it to become the new Empire in only a thousand years. The Foundation stories tell the tale of that 1000 years. <br /><br />The first couple of books are good -- the Foundation is faced with huge challenges, the challenges are overcome, and then the holograph of Seldon turns up to tell everyone that it all had to work this way to lead on to Empire. Fun to read the lessons and then think to the experiences of ancient Rome, etc, and how they relate to Asimov's vision of history. However, I think Asimov makes two mistakes. First, the introduction of the Second Foundation -- I won't talk about it for those who haven't read the books, but it takes all the risk out of the stories I think. Second -- and this I think this is really the more serious problem -- the author runs out of material on the creation of Empire in about year 300 of the 1000 year spread. The Foundation is not as big as the Galactic Empire had been, but otherwise it seems to be running along smoothly. Asimov should have doled out the challenges a bit more carefully. And gathered even more lessons from Rome. <br /><br />Oh by the way -- the worlds of the future appear to be very male-centric. No female characters at all for many chapters: Asimov then introduces some heroines but they are fulfilling very traditional female roles. If that is the kind of thing that makes you grind your teeth, then these are not the books for you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6544483166381711790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156931598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156931598" />
    <a title="Andreas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5175491-andreas"><img alt="Andreas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528952480p2/5175491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156931598?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreas" href="/user/show/5175491-andreas">Andreas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156931598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11812149373656616847">The series consists of seven books. In order of internal chronology:<br/><br/> * Prelude to Foundation<br/> * Forward the Foundation<br/> * Foundation<br/> * Foundation and Empire<br/> * Second Foundation<br/> * Foundation’s Edge<br/> * Foundation and Earth<br/><br/>This is truly one of SciFi’s classics. The original trilogy (starting with Foundation) is widely considered to be one of the finest SciFi series ever written. The rest of the books are of equally high quality, except (in my opinion) for Forward the Foundation, which seems more like </span>
  <span id="freeText11812149373656616847" style="display:none">The series consists of seven books. In order of internal chronology:<br /><br /> * Prelude to Foundation<br /> * Forward the Foundation<br /> * Foundation<br /> * Foundation and Empire<br /> * Second Foundation<br /> * Foundation’s Edge<br /> * Foundation and Earth<br /><br />This is truly one of SciFi’s classics. The original trilogy (starting with Foundation) is widely considered to be one of the finest SciFi series ever written. The rest of the books are of equally high quality, except (in my opinion) for Forward the Foundation, which seems more like an attempt to tie up loose ends, something of an obsession with Asimov towards the end of his career. Interestingly enough, the man who is arguably the main character, psychohistorian Hari Seldon, is long dead in most of the books. Few series convey a sense of evolving history as this one does, and at least the original three should be a must read for any Science Fiction fan.<br /><br />So why not a higher score? Well, I feel that although it is a classic and very good, it did not quite capture my imagination as much as some other books have.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.books.rosboch.net/?p=360">http://www.books.rosboch.net/?p=360</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11812149373656616847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/ijJpheygSoJU4AKxy0zuy6mbFt3pFrN1K40wgFnQt9k6oGY0GPZVC6Zu43otmNp7cG08vewieZELv02qSZ1lA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bSRkyWMMGATNCo3gnw8M5xFiJaOALoyuVkbfEvpoeuD35iz3pN1AeurAtmewlFw10gX9CgA6X4XGxhbmUilNqw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov">About Isaac Asimov</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1341965730p3/16667.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov">Isaac Asimov
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
19,207
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16663923884061593839">Isaac Asimov was a Russian-born, American author, a professor of biochemistry, and a highly successful writer, best known for his works of science fiction and for his popular science books.<br/><br/>Professor Asimov is generally considered one of the most prolific writers of all time, having written or edited more than 500 books and an estimated 90,000 letters and postcards. He has works published in nine o</span>
  <span id="freeText16663923884061593839" style="display:none">Isaac Asimov was a Russian-born, American author, a professor of biochemistry, and a highly successful writer, best known for his works of science fiction and for his popular science books.<br /><br />Professor Asimov is generally considered one of the most prolific writers of all time, having written or edited more than 500 books and an estimated 90,000 letters and postcards. He has works published in nine of the ten major categories of the Dewey Decimal System (lacking only an entry in the 100s category of Philosophy).<br /><br />Asimov is widely considered a master of the science-fiction genre and, along with Robert A. Heinlein and Arthur C. Clarke, was considered one of the "Big Three" science-fiction writers during his lifetime. Asimov's most famous work is the Foundation Series; his other major series are the Galactic Empire series and the Robot series, both of which he later tied into the same fictional universe as the Foundation Series to create a unified "future history" for his stories much like those pioneered by Robert A. Heinlein and previously produced by Cordwainer Smith and Poul Anderson. He penned numerous short stories, among them "Nightfall", which in 1964 was voted by the Science Fiction Writers of America the best short science fiction story of all time, a title many still honor. He also wrote mysteries and fantasy, as well as a great amount of nonfiction. Asimov wrote the Lucky Starr series of juvenile science-fiction novels using the pen name Paul French.<br /><br />Most of Asimov's popularized science books explain scientific concepts in a historical way, going as far back as possible to a time when the science in question was at its simplest stage. He often provides nationalities, birth dates, and death dates for the scientists he mentions, as well as etymologies and pronunciation guides for technical terms. Examples include his Guide to Science, the three volume set Understanding Physics, and Asimov's Chronology of Science and Discovery.<br /><br />Asimov was a long-time member and Vice President of Mensa International, albeit reluctantly; he described some members of that organization as "brain-proud and aggressive about their IQs" He took more joy in being president of the American Humanist Association. The asteroid 5020 Asimov, the magazine Asimov's Science Fiction, a Brooklyn, NY elementary school, and two different Isaac Asimov Awards are named in his honor.<br /><br />----------------------------------------<br /><i>Isaac Asimov. (2007, November 29). In Wikipedia, The Free Encyclopedia. Retrieved 21:50, November 29, 2007, from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Asimov">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_As...</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16663923884061593839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
